<p><b>Ban Ki-moon</b> (<a href="/wiki/Hangul" title="Hangul">Hangul</a>:&#160;<span lang="ko-Hang">반기문</span>; <a href="/wiki/Hanja" title="Hanja">Hanja</a>:&#160;<span lang="ko-Hani">潘基文</span>; <small>Korean pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Korean" title="Help:IPA for Korean">[pan.ɡi.mun]</a></span>; born 13 June 1944) is a <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korean</a> diplomat who was the eighth <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> from January 2007 to December 2016. Before becoming Secretary-General, Ban was a career diplomat in South Korea's <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(South_Korea)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (South Korea)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a> and in the United Nations. He entered <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_service" title="Diplomatic service">diplomatic service</a> the year he graduated from university, accepting his first post in <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="New Delhi, India">New Delhi, India</a>.</p>
<p>Ban was the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_minister" title="Foreign minister">foreign minister</a> of <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> from January 2004 to November 2006. In February 2006 he began to campaign for the office of Secretary-General. Ban was initially considered to be a long shot for the office. As foreign minister of South Korea, however, he was able to travel to all the countries on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>, a maneuver that turned him into the campaign's front runner.</p>
<p>On 13 October 2006, he was elected to be the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations#List_of_Secretaries-General" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">eighth Secretary-General</a> by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>. On 1 January 2007, he succeeded <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>. As Secretary-General, he was responsible for several major reforms on peacekeeping and UN employment practices. Diplomatically, Ban has taken particularly strong views on <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>, pressing the issue repeatedly with U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>, and on the <a href="/wiki/Darfur_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Darfur conflict">Darfur conflict</a>, where he helped persuade Sudanese president <a href="/wiki/Omar_al-Bashir" title="Omar al-Bashir">Omar al-Bashir</a> to allow peacekeeping troops to enter <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian1-27_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian1-27-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WPost4-17_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPost4-17-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ban was named the world's 32nd most powerful person by the <a href="/wiki/Forbes_list_of_The_World%27s_Most_Powerful_People" title="Forbes list of The World's Most Powerful People"><i>Forbes</i> list of The World's Most Powerful People</a> in 2013, the highest among South Koreans.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> In 2014, he was named the third most powerful South Korean after <a href="/wiki/Lee_Kun-hee" title="Lee Kun-hee">Lee Kun-hee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lee_Jae-yong_(businessman)" title="Lee Jae-yong (businessman)">Lee Jae-yong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> In 2016, <i><a href="/wiki/Foreign_Policy" title="Foreign Policy">Foreign Policy</a></i> named Ban one of the <a href="/wiki/FP_Top_100_Global_Thinkers" title="FP Top 100 Global Thinkers">Top 100 Global Thinkers</a> for his achievement of making the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a> a legally binding treaty less than a year after it was adopted.<sup id="cite_ref-fpgt2016_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fpgt2016-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a> was <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretary-General_selection,_2016" title="United Nations Secretary-General selection, 2016">appointed by the General Assembly on 13 October 2016</a> to be the successor of Ban Ki-moon as he stepped down on 31 December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> He was widely considered to be a potential candidate for the <a href="/wiki/South_Korean_presidential_election,_2017" title="South Korean presidential election, 2017">2017 South Korean presidential election</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> before announcing, on February 1, that he would not be running.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">Early life and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ban was born on 13 June 1944 in the small farming village of Haengchi, Wonnam Township (<i>-myeon</i>), in <a href="/wiki/Eumseong_County" title="Eumseong County">Eumseong County</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Chungcheong_Province" title="North Chungcheong Province">North Chungcheong Province</a> in <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eumseong.go.kr_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eumseong.go.kr-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Times12-09_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times12-09-11">[11]</a></sup> His family then moved to the nearby town of <a href="/wiki/Chungju" title="Chungju">Chungju</a>, where he grew up.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_12-22_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_12-22-12">[12]</a></sup> During Ban's childhood, his father had a warehouse business, but the warehouse went bankrupt and the family lost its middle-class standard of living. When Ban was six, his family fled to a remote mountainside for much of the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Times12-09_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times12-09-11">[11]</a></sup> After the war ended, his family returned to <a href="/wiki/Chungju" title="Chungju">Chungju</a>. Ban has said that, during this time, he met <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">American soldiers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT10-09_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT10-09-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>In secondary school (<a href="/wiki/Chungju_High_School" title="Chungju High School">Chungju High School</a>), Ban became a star student, particularly in his studies of the <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a>. In 1962, Ban won an essay contest sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">Red Cross</a> and earned a trip to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> where he lived in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="San Francisco, California">San Francisco</a> with a host family for several months.<sup id="cite_ref-FT10-10_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT10-10-14">[14]</a></sup> As part of the trip, Ban met U.S. President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Times12-09_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times12-09-11">[11]</a></sup> When a journalist at the meeting asked Ban what he wanted to be when he grew up, he said, "I want to become a diplomat."<sup id="cite_ref-LAT10-09_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT10-09-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>He received a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">bachelor's degree</a> in <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a> from <a href="/wiki/Seoul_National_University" title="Seoul National University">Seoul National University</a> in 1970, and earned a <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Public_Administration" title="Master of Public Administration">Master of Public Administration</a> from the <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_School_of_Government" title="John F. Kennedy School of Government">John F. Kennedy School of Government</a> at <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> in 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT10-09_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT10-09-13">[13]</a></sup> At Harvard, he studied under <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Nye" title="Joseph Nye">Joseph Nye</a>, who remarked that Ban had "a rare combination of analytic clarity, humility and perseverance".<sup id="cite_ref-FT10-10_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT10-10-14">[14]</a></sup> Ban was awarded the degree of <a href="/wiki/Honorary_Degree" class="mw-redirect" title="Honorary Degree">Doctor of Laws (Honoris Causa)</a> by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Malta" title="University of Malta">University of Malta</a> on 22 April 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-UOM04-17_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UOM04-17-15">[15]</a></sup> He further received an honorary degree of Doctor of Laws from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington" title="University of Washington">University of Washington</a> in October 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> an honorary degree of Doctor of Law from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a> in February 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and an Honorary Doctor of Humane Letters Degree from <a href="/wiki/Loyola_Marymount_University" title="Loyola Marymount University">Loyola Marymount University</a> in April 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> On 30 August 2016, he was conferred the Honorary Doctor of Letters by <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Singapore" title="National University of Singapore">National University of Singapore</a> for his lifetime of service to humanity.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to his native <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>, Ban speaks <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>. According to a retired UN official, "one of Ban's biggest handicaps was his lack of fluency in English, which made it difficult for him to win over audiences in the US and elsewhere."<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> There have also been questions, however, regarding the extent of his knowledge of French, one of the two <a href="/wiki/Working_language" title="Working language">working languages</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretariat" title="United Nations Secretariat">United Nations Secretariat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Phoney_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Phoney-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diplomatic_career">Diplomatic career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Diplomatic career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ban_Ki-moon_and_Condoleezza_Rice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ban_Ki-moon_and_Condoleezza_Rice.jpg/220px-Ban_Ki-moon_and_Condoleezza_Rice.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ban_Ki-moon_and_Condoleezza_Rice.jpg/330px-Ban_Ki-moon_and_Condoleezza_Rice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ban_Ki-moon_and_Condoleezza_Rice.jpg/440px-Ban_Ki-moon_and_Condoleezza_Rice.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="418" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ban_Ki-moon_and_Condoleezza_Rice.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ban_Ki-moon,_Mrs_Ban,_Peter_Kr%C3%A4mer_and_Jaka_Bizilj.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Ban Ki-moon, Mrs Ban, Peter Krämer and Jaka Bizilj.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Ban_Ki-moon%2C_Mrs_Ban%2C_Peter_Kr%C3%A4mer_and_Jaka_Bizilj.jpg/220px-Ban_Ki-moon%2C_Mrs_Ban%2C_Peter_Kr%C3%A4mer_and_Jaka_Bizilj.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Ban_Ki-moon%2C_Mrs_Ban%2C_Peter_Kr%C3%A4mer_and_Jaka_Bizilj.jpg/330px-Ban_Ki-moon%2C_Mrs_Ban%2C_Peter_Kr%C3%A4mer_and_Jaka_Bizilj.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Ban_Ki-moon%2C_Mrs_Ban%2C_Peter_Kr%C3%A4mer_and_Jaka_Bizilj.jpg/440px-Ban_Ki-moon%2C_Mrs_Ban%2C_Peter_Kr%C3%A4mer_and_Jaka_Bizilj.jpg 2x" data-file-width="852" data-file-height="567" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ban_Ki-moon,_Mrs_Ban,_Peter_Kr%C3%A4mer_and_Jaka_Bizilj.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
Ban Ki-moon with <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">U.S. Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a> in January 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After graduating from university, Ban received the top score on Korea's foreign service exam. He joined the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_South_Korea" title="Foreign relations of South Korea">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a> in May 1970 and worked his way up the career ladder during the years of the <a href="/wiki/Yusin_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Yusin Constitution">Yusin Constitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FT10-10_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT10-10-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ban's first overseas posting was to <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi" title="New Delhi">New Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, where he served as vice consul and impressed many of his superiors in the foreign ministry with his competence. Ban reportedly accepted a posting to India rather than the United States, because in India he would be able to save more money to send to his family.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCprofile_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCprofile-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KH_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KH-23">[23]</a></sup> In 1974 he received his first posting to the United Nations, as First Secretary of the South Permanent Observer Mission (South Korea became a full UN member-state on 17 September 1991).<sup id="cite_ref-NYT10-03_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT10-03-24">[24]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/Park_Chung-hee" title="Park Chung-hee">Park Chung-hee</a>'s 1979 assassination, Ban assumed the post of Director of the United Nations Division.</p>
<p>In 1980 Ban became director of the United Nations' International Organizations and Treaties Bureau, headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KH_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KH-23">[23]</a></sup> He has been posted twice to the South Korean embassy in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> Between these two assignments he served as Director-General for American Affairs in 1990–92. In 1992, he became Vice Chairman of the South-North Joint Nuclear Control Commission, following the adoption by South and <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> of the Joint Declaration of the Denuclearization of the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Peninsula" title="Korean Peninsula">Korean Peninsula</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCprofile_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCprofile-22">[22]</a></sup> From 1993 to 1994 Ban was Korea's deputy ambassador to the United States. He was promoted to the position of Deputy Minister for Policy Planning and International Organizations in 1995 and then appointed National Security Advisor to the President in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-KH_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KH-23">[23]</a></sup> Ban's lengthy career overseas has been credited with helping him avoid South Korea's unforgiving political environment.<sup id="cite_ref-Time_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ban was appointed <a href="/wiki/Ambassador" title="Ambassador">Ambassador</a> to <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> in 1998, and a year later he was also elected as Chairman of the Preparatory Commission for the <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_Nuclear-Test-Ban_Treaty_Organization" title="Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty Organization">Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty Organization</a> (CTBTO PrepCom). During the negotiations, in what Ban considers the biggest blunder of his career, he included in a public letter a positive statement about the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Ballistic_Missile_Treaty" title="Anti-Ballistic Missile Treaty">Anti-Ballistic Missile Treaty</a> in 2001, not long after the United States had decided to abandon the treaty. To avoid anger from the United States, Ban was fired by President <a href="/wiki/Kim_Dae-jung" title="Kim Dae-jung">Kim Dae-jung</a>, who also issued a public apology for Ban's statement.<sup id="cite_ref-Times12-09_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times12-09-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ban was unemployed for the only time in his career and was expecting to receive an assignment to work in a remote and unimportant embassy.<sup id="cite_ref-Times12-09_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times12-09-11">[11]</a></sup> In 2001, during the 56th Session of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>, South Korea held the rotating presidency, and to Ban's surprise, he was selected to be the chief of staff to general assembly president <a href="/wiki/Han_Seung-soo" title="Han Seung-soo">Han Seung-soo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Times10-14_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times10-14-26">[26]</a></sup> In 2003, incoming president <a href="/wiki/Roh_Moo-hyun" title="Roh Moo-hyun">Roh Moo-hyun</a> selected Ban as one of his foreign policy advisors.<sup id="cite_ref-KH_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KH-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_minister_of_South_Korea">Foreign minister of South Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Foreign minister of South Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2004, Ban replaced <a href="/wiki/Yoon_Young-kwan" title="Yoon Young-kwan">Yoon Young-kwan</a> as foreign minister of South Korea under president <a href="/wiki/Roh_Moo-hyun" title="Roh Moo-hyun">Roh Moo-hyun</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT10-09_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT10-09-13">[13]</a></sup> At the beginning of his term, Ban was faced with two major crises: in June 2004 <a href="/wiki/Kim_Sun-il" title="Kim Sun-il">Kim Sun-il</a>, a South Korean working as an Arabic translator, was kidnapped and killed in Iraq by <a href="/wiki/Islamism" title="Islamism">Islamic extremists</a>; and in December 2004 dozens of Koreans died in the <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake">2004 Indian Ocean tsunami</a>. Ban survived scrutiny from lawmakers and saw an upturn in his popularity when talks began with North Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-KH_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KH-23">[23]</a></sup> Ban became actively involved in issues relating to North-South Korean relationships.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCprofile_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCprofile-22">[22]</a></sup> In September 2005, as <a href="/wiki/Foreign_minister" title="Foreign minister">foreign minister</a>, he played a leading role in the diplomatic efforts to adopt the Joint Statement on resolving the North Korean nuclear issue at the Fourth Round of the <a href="/wiki/Six-party_talks" title="Six-party talks">Six-party talks</a> held in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Official_Bio_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Bio-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Newsweek_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newsweek-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>As foreign minister, Ban oversaw the trade and aid policies of South Korea. This work put Ban in the position of signing trade deals and delivering foreign assistance to diplomats who would later be influential in his candidacy for Secretary-General. For example, Ban became the first senior South Korean minister to travel to the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> since its independence in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-WashPost0929_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashPost0929-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Nations_career">United Nations career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: United Nations career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campaign_for_Secretary-General:_2007">Campaign for Secretary-General: 2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Campaign for Secretary-General: 2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<td><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia"><img alt="Latvia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Flag_of_Latvia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Latvia.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Flag_of_Latvia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Latvia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Flag_of_Latvia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Latvia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span></td>

<a href="/wiki/Kabul_University" title="Kabul University">Kabul University</a>, Afghanistan</td>

<td><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand"><img alt="Thailand" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/23px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/35px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/45px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span></td>

<td>Deputy prime minister<br />
of Thailand</td>

<tr>
<td><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan"><img alt="Jordan" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Flag_of_Jordan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Jordan.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Flag_of_Jordan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Jordan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Flag_of_Jordan.svg/46px-Flag_of_Jordan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="840" data-file-height="420" /></a></span></td>

<td>Jordan's ambassador<br />
to the United Nations</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka"><img alt="Sri Lanka" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Flag_of_Sri_Lanka.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sri_Lanka.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Flag_of_Sri_Lanka.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sri_Lanka.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Flag_of_Sri_Lanka.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sri_Lanka.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Jayantha_Dhanapala" title="Jayantha Dhanapala">Jayantha Dhanapala</a></td>
<td>Former Under-Secretary-General<br />
for disarmament; from Sri Lanka</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In February 2006, Ban declared his candidacy to replace <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a> as UN Secretary-General at the end of 2006, becoming the first South Korean to run for the office.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Though Ban was the first to announce a candidacy, he was not originally considered a serious contender.<sup id="cite_ref-FT10-10_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT10-10-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over the next eight months, Ban made ministerial visits to each of the 15 countries with a seat on the Security Council.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT10-09_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT10-09-13">[13]</a></sup> Of the seven candidates, he topped each of the four <a href="/wiki/Straw_poll" title="Straw poll">straw polls</a> conducted by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>: on 24 July,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> 14 September,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> 28 September,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> and 2 October.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the period in which these polls took place, Ban made major speeches to the <a href="/wiki/Asia_Society" title="Asia Society">Asia Society</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Council_on_Foreign_Relations" title="Council on Foreign Relations">Council on Foreign Relations</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> To be confirmed, Ban needed not only to win the support of the diplomatic community, but also to be able to avoid a veto from any of the five permanent members of the council: <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. Ban was popular in Washington for having pushed to send South Korean troops to Iraq, and had the support of the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_George_W._Bush" title="Presidency of George W. Bush">Bush administration</a> as he pursued the position.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> But Ban also opposed several U.S. positions: he expressed his support for the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> and favoured an entirely non-confrontational approach to dealing with North Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT10-09_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT10-09-13">[13]</a></sup> Ban said during his campaign that he would like to visit North Korea in person to meet with <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jong-il" title="Kim Jong-il">Kim Jong-il</a> directly.<sup id="cite_ref-Newsweek_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newsweek-28">[28]</a></sup> Ban was viewed as a stark contrast from Kofi Annan, who was considered charismatic, but perceived as a weak manager because of problems surrounding the UN's oil-for-food program in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Economist10-07_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist10-07-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ban struggled to win the approval of France. His official biography states that he speaks both <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, the two working languages of the UN Secretariat. However, he has repeatedly struggled to answer questions in French from journalists.<sup id="cite_ref-Phoney_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Phoney-21">[21]</a></sup> Ban has repeatedly acknowledged his limitations at French, but assured French diplomats that he was devoted to continuing his study. At a press conference on 11 January 2007, Ban remarked, "My French perhaps could be improved, and I am continuing to work. I have taken French lessons over the last few months. I think that, even if my French isn't perfect, I will continue to study it."<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the Secretary-General election drew closer, there was rising criticism of the South Korean campaign on Ban's behalf. Specifically, his alleged practice of systematically visiting all member states of the Security Council in his role as the Minister of Foreign Affairs and Trade to secure votes in his support by signing trade deals with European countries and pledging <a href="/wiki/Aid" title="Aid">aid</a> to <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a> were the focus of many news articles.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>, "rivals have privately grumbled that Republic of Korea, which has the world's 11th-largest economy, has wielded its economic might to generate support for his candidacy". Ban reportedly said that these insinuations were "groundless". In an interview on 17 September 2006 he stated: "As front-runner, I know that I can become a target of this very scrutinizing process", and that he was "a man of integrity".<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the final informal poll on 2 October, Ban received fourteen favorable votes and one abstention ("no opinion") from the fifteen members of the Security Council. The one abstention came from the Japanese delegation, who <a href="/wiki/Japan%E2%80%93Korea_disputes" title="Japan–Korea disputes">vehemently opposed</a> the idea of a Korean taking the role of Secretary-General. Due to the overwhelming support of Ban by the rest of the Security Council, Japan later voted in favor of Ban to avoid controversy. More importantly, Ban was the only one to escape a veto; each of the other candidates received at least one "no" vote from among the five permanent members. After the vote, Shashi Tharoor, who finished second, withdrew his candidacy<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> and China's <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Representative" class="mw-redirect" title="Permanent Representative">Permanent Representative</a> to the UN told reporters that "it is quite clear from today's straw poll that Minister Ban Ki-moon is the candidate that the Security Council will recommend to the General Assembly".<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 9 October, the Security Council formally chose Ban as its nominee. In the public vote, he was supported by all 15 members of the council.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT10-10_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT10-10-45">[45]</a></sup> On 13 October, the 192-member <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">General Assembly</a> <a href="/wiki/Acclamation" title="Acclamation">acclaimed</a> Ban as Secretary-General.<sup id="cite_ref-Times10-14_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times10-14-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_term_as_Secretary-General">First term as Secretary-General</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: First term as Secretary-General">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_9_April_2008-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Vladimir_Putin_9_April_2008-1.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_9_April_2008-1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Vladimir_Putin_9_April_2008-1.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_9_April_2008-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Vladimir_Putin_9_April_2008-1.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_9_April_2008-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="334" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_9_April_2008-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ban Ki-moon with the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">President of Russia</a> <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> on 9 April 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:187px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ban_Ki-moon_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008_numb2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Ban_Ki-moon_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008_numb2.jpg/185px-Ban_Ki-moon_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008_numb2.jpg" width="185" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Ban_Ki-moon_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008_numb2.jpg/278px-Ban_Ki-moon_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008_numb2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Ban_Ki-moon_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008_numb2.jpg/371px-Ban_Ki-moon_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008_numb2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3405" data-file-height="4096" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ban_Ki-moon_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008_numb2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ban Ki-moon at Davos, Switzerland in the World Economic Forum.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>When Ban became Secretary-General, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> listed the major challenges facing him in 2007: "rising nuclear demons in <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and North Korea, a haemorrhaging wound in <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a>, unending violence in the Middle East, looming environmental disaster, escalating international terrorism, the proliferation of <a href="/wiki/Weapons_of_mass_destruction" class="mw-redirect" title="Weapons of mass destruction">weapons of mass destruction</a>, the spread of <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>. And then the more parochial concerns, such as the largely unfinished business of the most sweeping attempt at reform in the UN's history".<sup id="cite_ref-Econ01-06_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Econ01-06-46">[46]</a></sup> Before starting, Kofi Annan shared the story that when the first Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Trygve_Lie" title="Trygve Lie">Trygve Lie</a> left office, he told his successor, <a href="/wiki/Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld" title="Dag Hammarskjöld">Dag Hammarskjöld</a>, "You are about to take over the most impossible job on earth".<sup id="cite_ref-Times10-14_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times10-14-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 23 January 2007 Ban took office as the eighth Secretary-General of the United Nations. Ban's term as Secretary-General opened with a flap. At his first encounter with the press as Secretary-General on 2 January 2007, he refused to condemn the <a href="/wiki/Death_penalty" class="mw-redirect" title="Death penalty">death penalty</a> imposed on <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a> by the Iraqi High Tribunal, remarking, "The issue of capital punishment is for each and every member State to decide".<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Ban's statements contradicted long-standing United Nations opposition to the death penalty as a human-rights concern.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT01-03_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT01-03-48">[48]</a></sup> He quickly clarified his stance in the case of <a href="/wiki/Barzan_al-Tikriti" class="mw-redirect" title="Barzan al-Tikriti">Barzan al-Tikriti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Awad_al-Bandar" class="mw-redirect" title="Awad al-Bandar">Awad al-Bandar</a>, two top officials who were convicted of the deaths of 148 <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia Muslims</a> in the Iraqi village of <a href="/wiki/Dujail" title="Dujail">Dujail</a> in the 1980s. In a statement through his spokesperson on 6 January, he "strongly urged the Government of Iraq to grant a stay of execution to those whose death sentences may be carried out in the near future".<sup id="cite_ref-FT02-01_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT02-01-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> On the broader issue, he told a Washington, D.C. audience on 16 January 2007 that he recognized and encouraged the "growing trend in international society, international law and domestic policies and practices to phase out eventually the death penalty".<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This article needs to be <b>updated</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(October 2013)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On the tenth anniversary of <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Pol_Pot" title="Pol Pot">Pol Pot</a>'s death, 15 April 2008, Ban Ki-moon appealed for the senior leaders of the regime to be brought to justice. The <a href="/wiki/Extraordinary_Chambers_in_the_Courts_of_Cambodia" class="mw-redirect" title="Extraordinary Chambers in the Courts of Cambodia">Extraordinary Chambers in the Courts of Cambodia</a>-tribunal, which was established by both the United Nations and <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> and which became operational in 2006, is expected to continue until at least 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ban has received strong criticism from the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_of_Internal_Oversight_Services" title="United Nations Office of Internal Oversight Services">UN Office of Internal Oversight Services</a> (OIOS), which stated that the secretariat under Ban's leadership was "drifting into irrelevance".<sup id="cite_ref-OIOS_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OIOS-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cabinet">Cabinet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Cabinet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In early January, Ban appointed the key members of his cabinet. As his <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Deputy_Secretary-General" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Deputy Secretary-General">Deputy Secretary-General</a>, he selected <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzanian</a> foreign minister and professor <a href="/wiki/Asha-Rose_Migiro" title="Asha-Rose Migiro">Asha-Rose Migiro</a>, a move that pleased African diplomats who had concerns of losing power without Annan in office.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>The top position devoted exclusively to management, Under-Secretary-General for Management, was filled by <a href="/wiki/Alicia_B%C3%A1rcena_Ibarra" title="Alicia Bárcena Ibarra">Alicia Bárcena Ibarra</a> of Mexico. Bárcena was considered a UN insider, having previously served as Annan's chief of staff. Her appointment was seen by critics as an indication that Ban would not make dramatic changes to UN bureaucracy.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT01-04_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT01-04-55">[55]</a></sup> Ban appointed <a href="/wiki/John_Holmes_(British_diplomat)" title="John Holmes (British diplomat)">Sir John Holmes</a>, the British Ambassador to France, as <a href="/wiki/Under-Secretary-General_for_Humanitarian_Affairs_and_Emergency_Relief_Coordinator" title="Under-Secretary-General for Humanitarian Affairs and Emergency Relief Coordinator">Under-Secretary-General for humanitarian affairs and coordinator of emergency relief</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT01-04_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT01-04-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ban initially said that he would delay making other appointments until his first round of reforms were approved, yet later abandoned this idea after receiving criticism.<sup id="cite_ref-FT02-01_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT02-01-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT02-06_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT02-06-56">[56]</a></sup> In February he continued with appointments, selecting <a href="/wiki/B._Lynn_Pascoe" title="B. Lynn Pascoe">B. Lynn Pascoe</a>, the U.S. ambassador to Indonesia, to become Under-Secretary-General for political affairs. <a href="/wiki/Jean-Marie_Gu%C3%A9henno" title="Jean-Marie Guéhenno">Jean-Marie Guéhenno</a>, a French diplomat, who had served as Under-Secretary-General for peacekeeping operations under Annan, remained in office. Ban selected <a href="/wiki/Vijay_K._Nambiar" title="Vijay K. Nambiar">Vijay K. Nambiar</a> as his chief of staff.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT02-10_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT02-10-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>The appointment of many women to top jobs was seen as fulfilling a campaign promise Ban had made to increase the role of women in the United Nations. During Ban's first year as Secretary-General, more top jobs were being handled by women than ever before. Though not appointed by Ban, the president of the General Assembly, <a href="/wiki/Haya_Rashed_Al-Khalifa" title="Haya Rashed Al-Khalifa">Haya Rashed Al-Khalifa</a>, is only the third woman to hold this position in United Nations history.<sup id="cite_ref-CT04-11_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CT04-11-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reform_agenda">Reform agenda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Reform agenda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During his first month in office, Ban proposed two major reforms: to split the UN peacekeeping operation into two departments and to combine the political affairs and disarmament department. His proposals were met with stiff resistance from members of the UN General Assembly who bristled under Ban's request for rapid approval. The proposed merger of the disarmament and political affairs offices was criticized by many in the developing world, partially because of rumours that Ban hoped to place American B. Lynn Pascoe in charge of the new office. <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_D._Wolff" class="mw-redirect" title="Alejandro D. Wolff">Alejandro D. Wolff</a>, then acting American ambassador, said the United States backed his proposals.<sup id="cite_ref-FT02-01_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT02-01-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT02-06_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT02-06-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ban_Ki-moon_and_Bill_Gates_World_Economic_Forum_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ban_Ki-moon_and_Bill_Gates_World_Economic_Forum_2013.jpg/220px-Ban_Ki-moon_and_Bill_Gates_World_Economic_Forum_2013.jpg" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ban_Ki-moon_and_Bill_Gates_World_Economic_Forum_2013.jpg/330px-Ban_Ki-moon_and_Bill_Gates_World_Economic_Forum_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ban_Ki-moon_and_Bill_Gates_World_Economic_Forum_2013.jpg/440px-Ban_Ki-moon_and_Bill_Gates_World_Economic_Forum_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4516" data-file-height="2720" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ban_Ki-moon_and_Bill_Gates_World_Economic_Forum_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ban Ki-moon with <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a>, World Economic Forum, 24 January 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the early bout of reproach, Ban began extensive consultation with UN ambassadors, agreeing to have his peacekeeping proposal extensively vetted. After the consultations, Ban dropped his proposal to combine political affairs and disarmament.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT02-19_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT02-19-59">[59]</a></sup> Ban nevertheless pressed ahead with reforms on job requirements at the UN requiring that all positions be considered five-year appointments, all receive strict annual performance reviews, and all financial disclosures be made public. Though unpopular in the New York office, the move was popular in other UN offices around the world and lauded by UN observers.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT02-28_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT02-28-60">[60]</a></sup> Ban's proposal to split the peacekeeping operation into one group handling operations and another handling arms was finally adopted in mid-March 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-IrishTimes_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishTimes-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Key_issues">Key issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Key issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Secretary-General of the United Nations has the ability to influence debate on nearly any global issue. Although unsuccessful in some areas, Ban's predecessor Annan had been successful in increasing the UN peacekeeping presence and in popularizing the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a>. UN observers were eager to see on which issues Ban intended to focus, in addition to his declared interest in reforming the United Nations bureaucracy.<sup id="cite_ref-Econ01-06_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Econ01-06-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>On several prominent issues, such as proliferation in Iran and North Korea, Ban has deferred to the Security Council.<sup id="cite_ref-IrishTimes_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishTimes-61">[61]</a></sup> In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Nauru" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Nauru">Republic of Nauru</a> raised the issue of allowing the Republic of China (Taiwan) to sign the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Elimination_of_All_Forms_of_Discrimination_Against_Women" title="Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination Against Women">Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination Against Women</a>. Ban referenced the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_2758" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 2758">United Nations General Assembly Resolution 2758</a>, and refused the motion. On 19 July 2007, Taiwanese President <a href="/wiki/Chen_Shui-bian" title="Chen Shui-bian">Chen Shui-bian</a> wrote to request admission into the UN by the name Taiwan. Ban rejected the request, stating that Resolution 2758 defined Taiwan as part of China.<sup id="cite_ref-Taipei_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taipei-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_warming">Global warming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Global warming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20061017-1_d-0298-2-515h.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/20061017-1_d-0298-2-515h.jpg/220px-20061017-1_d-0298-2-515h.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/20061017-1_d-0298-2-515h.jpg/330px-20061017-1_d-0298-2-515h.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/20061017-1_d-0298-2-515h.jpg/440px-20061017-1_d-0298-2-515h.jpg 2x" data-file-width="514" data-file-height="344" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20061017-1_d-0298-2-515h.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> talks with <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretary-General" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Secretary-General">United Nations Secretary-General</a> Ban Ki-moon of <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> in October 2006. In their early meetings, Ban stressed the importance of confronting global warming.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ban early on identified <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> as one of the key issues of his administration. In a <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> meeting with U.S. President George W. Bush in January, Ban urged Bush to take steps to curb <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions. On 1 March 2007 in a speech before the UN General Assembly, Ban emphasized his concerns about global warming. Ban stated, "For my generation, coming of age at the height of the Cold War, fear of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_winter" title="Nuclear winter">nuclear winter</a> seemed the leading <a href="/wiki/Existential_threat" class="mw-redirect" title="Existential threat">existential threat</a> on the horizon. But the danger posed by war to all humanity—and to our planet—is at least matched by <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-Wash03-02_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wash03-02-63">[63]</a></sup> (referring to <a href="/wiki/Global_Warming" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Warming">Global Warming</a>, see <a href="/wiki/P:GW" class="mw-redirect" title="P:GW">P:GW</a> portal). On 3 September 2009 he further emphasized his concerns at the World Climate Conference in Geneva, when he stated, "Our foot is stuck on the accelerator and we are heading towards an abyss".<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In September, 2014, Ban joined demonstrators in the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Climate_March" title="People's Climate March">People's Climate March</a> in New York City,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> and also called together world leaders for the UN Climate Summit,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> in preparation for the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Climate Change Conference">United Nations Climate Change Conference</a> to be held in Paris in late 2015.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_East">Middle East</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Middle East">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>On Thursday, 22 March 2007, while Ban was taking part in the first stop of a tour of the Middle East, a mortar attack hit just 80 meters (260&#160;ft) from where the Secretary-General was standing, interrupting a press conference in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Green_Zone" title="Green Zone">Green Zone</a>, and visibly shaking Ban and others. No one was hurt in the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The United Nations had already limited its role in Iraq after its Baghdad headquarters was bombed in August 2003, killing 22 people. Ban said, however, that he still hoped to find a way for the United Nations to "do more for Iraqi social and political development".<sup id="cite_ref-NYT03-24_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT03-24-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>On his trip, Ban visited <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, where Ban attended a conference with leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a> and met for several hours with <a href="/wiki/Omar_Hassan_al-Bashir" class="mw-redirect" title="Omar Hassan al-Bashir">Omar Hassan al-Bashir</a>, the Sudanese president who had resisted UN peacekeepers in Darfur.<sup id="cite_ref-IrishTimes_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishTimes-61">[61]</a></sup> While Ban met with <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">Mahmoud Abbas</a>, the Palestinian president, he declined to meet with <a href="/wiki/Ismail_Haniya" class="mw-redirect" title="Ismail Haniya">Ismail Haniya</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT04-03_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT04-03-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_at_the_34th_G8_Summit_7-9_July_2008-49.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Dmitry_Medvedev_at_the_34th_G8_Summit_7-9_July_2008-49.jpg/220px-Dmitry_Medvedev_at_the_34th_G8_Summit_7-9_July_2008-49.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Dmitry_Medvedev_at_the_34th_G8_Summit_7-9_July_2008-49.jpg/330px-Dmitry_Medvedev_at_the_34th_G8_Summit_7-9_July_2008-49.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Dmitry_Medvedev_at_the_34th_G8_Summit_7-9_July_2008-49.jpg/440px-Dmitry_Medvedev_at_the_34th_G8_Summit_7-9_July_2008-49.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="334" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_at_the_34th_G8_Summit_7-9_July_2008-49.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ban with <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a> at the <a href="/wiki/34th_G8_Summit" class="mw-redirect" title="34th G8 Summit">34th G8 Summit</a>, July 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ban Ki-moon criticized Israel on 10 March 2008 for planning to build housing units in a <a href="/wiki/West_Bank_settlement" class="mw-redirect" title="West Bank settlement">West Bank settlement</a>, saying the decision conflicts with "Israel's obligation under the road map" for Middle East peace.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>During a meeting of the <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council">UN Security Council</a> on Wednesday, 7 January 2009, Ban called for an immediate end to fighting in the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>. He criticized both sides, Israel for bombarding <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza</a> and Hamas for firing rockets into Israel.</p>
<p>Although the <a href="/wiki/2009_Iranian_presidential_election" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 Iranian presidential election">2009 Iranian presidential election</a> was widely disputed, Ban Ki-moon sent a traditional congratulation message<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> to the Iranian president upon his inauguration. He kept silent over the request of <a href="/wiki/Shirin_Ebadi" title="Shirin Ebadi">Shirin Ebadi</a> to visit<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Iran after the crackdown on peaceful post-election protests by the Iranian police, which was perceived as a <a href="/wiki/Crime_against_humanity" class="mw-redirect" title="Crime against humanity">crime against humanity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> More than 4,000 people were arrested and nearly 70 were killed, some while being held in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> In another incident, several prominent intellectuals, including <a href="/wiki/Akbar_Ganji" title="Akbar Ganji">Akbar Ganji</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamid_Dabashi" title="Hamid Dabashi">Hamid Dabashi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Noam_Chomsky" title="Noam Chomsky">Noam Chomsky</a>, went on a three-day <a href="/wiki/Hunger_strike" title="Hunger strike">hunger strike</a> in front of the UN. The incident was followed by an official request by more than 200 intellectuals, human rights activists and reformist politicians in Iran for the <a href="/wiki/UN" class="mw-redirect" title="UN">UN</a> reaction.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Ban Ki-moon however did not take any action to stop the violence in Iran.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hillary_Clinton_and_Ban_Ki-moon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Hillary_Clinton_and_Ban_Ki-moon.jpg/220px-Hillary_Clinton_and_Ban_Ki-moon.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Hillary_Clinton_and_Ban_Ki-moon.jpg/330px-Hillary_Clinton_and_Ban_Ki-moon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Hillary_Clinton_and_Ban_Ki-moon.jpg/440px-Hillary_Clinton_and_Ban_Ki-moon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="399" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hillary_Clinton_and_Ban_Ki-moon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> with Ban Ki-Moon, 7 April 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2011_Libyan_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Libyan Civil War">Libyan Civil War</a> began in 2011, the last year of Ban's first term, and dominated his attention and public statements that year. Throughout the conflict, he lobbied for peaceful solutions to the crisis. He frequently spoke out against military action in Libya, believing that a diplomatic solution would be possible and preferable. However, he conceded that if then-leader <a href="/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Muammar Gaddafi">Muammar Gaddafi</a> refused to abide by a cease fire agreement, the international coalition of military forces would have no choice but to intervene to protect the human rights of Libyans.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The Gaddafi government was eventually overthrown and Gaddafi killed in the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Darfur">Darfur</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Darfur">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Ban took the first foreign trip of his term to attend the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> summit in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, in January 2007 as part of an effort to reach out to the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">Group of 77</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Econ01-06_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Econ01-06-46">[46]</a></sup> He repeatedly identified Darfur as the top humanitarian priority of his administration.<sup id="cite_ref-IrishTimes_61-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishTimes-61">[61]</a></sup> Ban played a large role, with several face-to-face meetings with <a href="/wiki/President_of_Sudan" class="mw-redirect" title="President of Sudan">Sudanese President</a> <a href="/wiki/Omar_Hassan_al-Bashir" class="mw-redirect" title="Omar Hassan al-Bashir">Omar Hassan al-Bashir</a>, in convincing Sudan to allow UN peacekeepers to enter the Darfur region. On 31 July 2007 the United Nations Security Council approved sending 26,000 UN peacekeepers into the region to join 7,000 troops from the African Union. The resolution was heralded as a major breakthrough in confronting the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Darfur" title="War in Darfur">Darfur conflict</a> (although the United States labeled the conflict a "<a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>", the United Nations has declined to do so). The first phase of the peacekeeping mission began in October 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-NPR08-02_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR08-02-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Myanmar">Myanmar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Myanmar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Ban Ki-moon flew to Myanmar on 25 May 2008 to guide a conference with international agencies aimed at boosting donations for the nation, which was struck by <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Nargis" title="Cyclone Nargis">Cyclone Nargis</a> on 2 May 2008. The conference was initiated after Ban had met with <a href="/wiki/Than_Shwe" title="Than Shwe">Than Shwe</a>, the leading figure of Myanmar's government 23 May 2008. Ban toured the devastation—especially in the hard-hit <a href="/wiki/Irrawaddy_Delta" title="Irrawaddy Delta">Irrawaddy Delta</a>—23 May 2008 and 24 May 2008. Myanmar officials agreed to allow the <a href="/wiki/Yangon_International_Airport" title="Yangon International Airport">Yangon International Airport</a> to be used as a logistical hub for aid distribution.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn-05-25-08_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-05-25-08-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campaign_for_second_term_as_Secretary-General:_2011">Campaign for second term as Secretary-General: 2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Campaign for second term as Secretary-General: 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 6 June 2011, Ban Ki-moon formally announced his candidacy for a second consecutive term as Secretary-General of the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-unAppointSecond_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unAppointSecond-80">[80]</a></sup> He announced his candidacy at a press conference, following a meeting with the Asian group of countries at the United Nations. Ban Ki-moon's first mandate as the Secretary-General was set to end on 31 December 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The five permanent Security Council members supported his candidacy. There was no declared rival for the post.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_term_as_Secretary-General">Second term as Secretary-General</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Second term as Secretary-General">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_laughs_with_U.N._Secretary-General_Ban_before_meeting_on_the_sidelines_of_Vibrant_Gujarat_Summit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Secretary_Kerry_laughs_with_U.N._Secretary-General_Ban_before_meeting_on_the_sidelines_of_Vibrant_Gujarat_Summit.jpg/220px-Secretary_Kerry_laughs_with_U.N._Secretary-General_Ban_before_meeting_on_the_sidelines_of_Vibrant_Gujarat_Summit.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Secretary_Kerry_laughs_with_U.N._Secretary-General_Ban_before_meeting_on_the_sidelines_of_Vibrant_Gujarat_Summit.jpg/330px-Secretary_Kerry_laughs_with_U.N._Secretary-General_Ban_before_meeting_on_the_sidelines_of_Vibrant_Gujarat_Summit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Secretary_Kerry_laughs_with_U.N._Secretary-General_Ban_before_meeting_on_the_sidelines_of_Vibrant_Gujarat_Summit.jpg/440px-Secretary_Kerry_laughs_with_U.N._Secretary-General_Ban_before_meeting_on_the_sidelines_of_Vibrant_Gujarat_Summit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2993" data-file-height="1990" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ban_Ki-moon,_Xi_Jinping_and_Barack_Obama_in_Hangzhou_(2016-09-03).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ban_Ki-moon%2C_Xi_Jinping_and_Barack_Obama_in_Hangzhou_%282016-09-03%29.jpg/220px-Ban_Ki-moon%2C_Xi_Jinping_and_Barack_Obama_in_Hangzhou_%282016-09-03%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ban_Ki-moon%2C_Xi_Jinping_and_Barack_Obama_in_Hangzhou_%282016-09-03%29.jpg/330px-Ban_Ki-moon%2C_Xi_Jinping_and_Barack_Obama_in_Hangzhou_%282016-09-03%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ban_Ki-moon%2C_Xi_Jinping_and_Barack_Obama_in_Hangzhou_%282016-09-03%29.jpg/440px-Ban_Ki-moon%2C_Xi_Jinping_and_Barack_Obama_in_Hangzhou_%282016-09-03%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
