Ban Ki-moon, Chinese President <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a>, and U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in Hangzhou, China, 3 September 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 17 June 2011, he received the recommendation of the Security Council by a unanimous vote,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> and, on 21 June, his nomination was confirmed by a unanimous<sup id="cite_ref-secondAppointUnan_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-secondAppointUnan-84">[84]</a></sup> acclamation vote at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> His new five-year term as Secretary-General commenced on 1 January 2012<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> and will end on 31 December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-unAppointSecond_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unAppointSecond-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cabinet_2">Cabinet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Cabinet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Ban appointed Swedish diplomat <a href="/wiki/Jan_Eliasson" title="Jan Eliasson">Jan Eliasson</a> as his new Deputy Secretary-General on 2 March 2012. His Chief of Staff is <a href="/wiki/Edmond_Mulet" title="Edmond Mulet">Edmond Mulet</a> of Guatemala. The appointments were part of Ban's commitment to replace top positions in his group for his second term.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Key_issues_2">Key issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Key issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Since beginning his second term in January 2012, Ban has focused his public statements and speeches on peace and equality in the Middle East and on equality issues.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_East_2">Middle East</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Middle East">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The aftermath of the Libyan Civil War and other events of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a> continued to command Ban's attention with the start of his second term. He focused in 2012 on what he termed "intolerance" in the Arab world. After travelling to <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> to participate in the opening of the <a href="/wiki/KAICIID_Dialogue_Centre" title="KAICIID Dialogue Centre">KAICIID Dialogue Centre</a> to foster interreligious dialogue, Ban commented, "Many countries in the Arab world including Saudi Arabia are changing. Since the Arab Spring, the leaders have begun to listen to the voice of their people." He was however criticised in the Austrian press for associating himself with a project of Saudi <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Abdullah of Saudi Arabia">King Abdullah</a>, Saudi Arabia being a location of perceived religious intolerance.<sup id="cite_ref-Die_Presse_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Die_Presse-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Throughout 2012, Ban expressed his concern about the continuing <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli–Palestinian conflict">Israeli–Palestinian conflict</a>, in particular the condition of the Palestinian <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_prisoners_in_Israel" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian prisoners in Israel">hunger strikers</a> in Israeli prisons<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> and the movement restrictions imposed on Gaza Strip residents.<sup id="cite_ref-Die_Presse_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Die_Presse-88">[88]</a></sup> On 30 August 2012 Ban criticized the Iranian leadership due to their statements regarding Israel's destruction and denying the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> On 16 August 2013, Ban Ki-moon admitted that the UN was biased against Israel, stating in a meeting with Israeli students that there was a biased attitude towards the Israeli people and Israeli government at the UN. He described this as "an unfortunate situation."<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> A few days later, he backtracked on the utterance.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> During an interview on 16 December, 2016, Ban said that the UN has issued a "disproportionate volume of resolutions, reports and conferences criticizing Israel."<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 26 January 2016, Ban made a statement in relation to the attacks by Palestinians against Israelis. Ban Ki-moon said that "as oppressed peoples have demonstrated throughout the ages, it is human nature to react to occupation, which often serves as a potent incubator of hate and extremism".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-94">[94]</a></sup> In rebuking Ban's statement, the Israeli PM <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu" title="Benjamin Netanyahu">Benjamin Netanyahu</a> stated that "there is no justification for terror".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ban has criticized <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> saying: "Grave violations against children increased dramatically as a result of the escalating conflict".<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> In June 2016, Ban Ki-moon removed a Saudi-led coalition from a list of <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_rights" title="Children's rights">children's rights</a> violators.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> He later admitted that <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> threatened to cut Palestinian aid and funds to other UN programs if coalition was not removed from blacklist for killing children in Yemen. According to one source, there was also a threat of "clerics in Riyadh meeting to issue a <a href="/wiki/Fatwa" title="Fatwa">fatwa</a> against the UN, declaring it anti-Muslim, which would mean no contacts of <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">OIC</a> members, no relations, contributions, support, to any UN projects, programs".<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukraine">Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ukraine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>On June 26, 2016, during a speech in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, Ban said Russia "has a critical role to play" in addressing global issues "from ending the conflicts in Ukraine and Syria, to safeguarding human rights and controlling the proliferation of weapons of mass destruction." His comments were condemned by <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine's</a> UN envoy <a href="/wiki/Volodymyr_Yelchenko" title="Volodymyr Yelchenko">Volodymyr Yelchenko</a>, saying that he doesn't understand how the UN chief "can say such things which sort of praise the role of Russia in settling the conflict in Ukraine when the Russian Federation is the main player in aggressing Ukraine and in keeping this conflict boiling." He also noted that Russia is being accused of human rights abuses in <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a> and is "building up the nuclear potential" on the peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT_rights">LGBT rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: LGBT rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>On 7 March 2012 Ban delivered a speech titled "The Time Has Come" to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">United Nations Human Rights Council</a> urging the Council to place greater emphasis on combating <a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">homophobia</a> and promoting <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="LGBT rights">LGBT rights</a> around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> The speech was met by a protest by a group of delegates, who organized a walk-out protest during the speech.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>During a speech at the UN headquarters commemorating Human Rights Day, Ban condemned countries with anti-gay laws, mentioning 76 countries that criminalize homosexuality. He said:</p>
<dl>
<dd>"It is an outrage that in our modern world, so many countries continue to criminalize people simply for loving another human being of the same sex."</dd>
</dl>
<p>Ban has told senior managers that homophobia will not be tolerated. He pointed to countries such as Ukraine which has proposed criminalizing public discussion about homosexuality as threatening basic human rights. He further stated that government has a duty to defend vulnerable minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> In April 2013, he described LGBT rights as one of the great neglected human rights of our time. He also said that religion, culture or tradition can never justify denial of basic rights.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Syrian_conflict">Syrian conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Syrian conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian Civil War</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Geneva_II_Conference_on_Syria" title="Geneva II Conference on Syria">Geneva II Conference on Syria</a></div>
<p>Ban has been organizing and moderating the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_II_Conference_on_Syria" title="Geneva II Conference on Syria">Geneva II Conference on Syria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_action">Humanitarian action</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Humanitarian action">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/World_Humanitarian_Summit" title="World Humanitarian Summit">World Humanitarian Summit</a></div>
<p>On 25 January 2012, Ban announced that he would convene the world's first summit on <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_aid" title="Humanitarian aid">humanitarian aid</a> in order to "share knowledge and establish common best practices."<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Known as the <a href="/wiki/World_Humanitarian_Summit" title="World Humanitarian Summit">World Humanitarian Summit</a>, the event took place in the 23rd–24 May 2016 in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. In preparation for the summit, Ban released a report on 9 February 2016 titled ‘One Humanity, Shared Responsibility’ in which he laid out an "Agenda for Humanity" based on consultations with more than 23,000 people in 153 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The Agenda for Humanity outlines what is needed to reform humanitarian action, including political leadership to prevent and end conflict, new forms of financing, and a shift from providing aid to ending need. The summit is scheduled to include 5,000 participants, including representatives from governments, NGOs, civil society organizations, and the private sector, as well as individuals affected by humanitarian crises.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_as_UN_Secretary-General">Criticism as UN Secretary-General</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Criticism as UN Secretary-General">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>, "some UN employees and delegates" expressed resentment at Ban's perceived <a href="/wiki/Favoritism" class="mw-disambig" title="Favoritism">favoritism</a> in the appointment of South Korean nationals in key posts. Previous UN chiefs such as <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Waldheim" title="Kurt Waldheim">Kurt Waldheim</a> (Austria), <a href="/wiki/Javier_P%C3%A9rez_de_Cu%C3%A9llar" title="Javier Pérez de Cuéllar">Javier Pérez de Cuéllar</a> (Peru) and <a href="/wiki/Boutros_Boutros-Ghali" title="Boutros Boutros-Ghali">Boutros Boutros-Ghali</a> (Egypt) brought small teams of trusted aides or clerical workers from their country's Foreign Ministry. But according to "some officials" in the <i>Post</i> story, Ban has gone further, boosting South Korea's presence in UN ranks by more than 20 percent during his first year in office. In response, Ban and his aides have claimed that allegations of favoritism are wrong, and that some of the harshest criticisms against him have undercurrents of <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fav_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fav-108">[108]</a></sup> He said that the South Korean nationals he had appointed—including <a href="/wiki/Choi_Young-jin" title="Choi Young-jin">Choi Young-jin</a>, who has served as a high-ranking official in the United Nations' peacekeeping department—are highly qualified for their positions. Others such as Donald P. Gregg, a former U.S. ambassador to South Korea, say the complaints are driven by envy, "I think being from South Korea, and people have growing respect for South Korea, that's a great enhancement for the secretary general. If he brings along talented people who (whom) he knows very well, I think that's also a plus." UN records show that South Korea, the organization's eleventh-largest financial contributor, had 54 South Korean nationals assigned to its mission six months before Ban took over the top UN post.<sup id="cite_ref-fav_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fav-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>Former UN Under Secretary General for Oversight Services <a href="/wiki/Inga-Britt_Ahlenius" title="Inga-Britt Ahlenius">Inga-Britt Ahlenius</a> denounced Ban Ki-moon after resigning her post in 2010, calling him reprehensible.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Ahlenius's critique was based on the grounds that the Secretary-General consistently made efforts to undermine the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Internal_Oversight_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Office of Internal Oversight Services">Office of Internal Oversight Services</a> (OIOS) mandate and challenge its operational independence.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> In particular, the two disputed Ahlenius's plans to hire a former prosecutor, Robert Appleton, who had carried out aggressive investigations into corruption in UN peacekeeping missions from 2006 to 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-111">[111]</a></sup> Ban's staff explained that Appleton's appointment was rejected because female candidates had not been properly considered, and said that the final selection should have been made by Ban, not Ahlenius.<sup id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-111">[111]</a></sup> However, Ahlenius countered in her End of Assignment memo that "for the Secretary-General to control appointments in OIOS is an infringement of the operational independence of OIOS", and further stated, "There is no transparency, there is lack of accountability. Rather than supporting the internal oversight which is the sign of strong leadership and good governance, you have strived to undermine its position and to control it. I do not see any signs of reform in the Organization."<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/ROKS_Cheonan_sinking" title="ROKS Cheonan sinking">ROKS <i>Cheonan</i> sinking</a> events, he took the step of demanding action against <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> for the alleged sinking of a vessel from his country. This was reported by U.N. Dispatch as being unusual, because it is rare for any Secretary-General—and particularly Ban Ki-moon—to comment on the Security Council taking action on an issue as his office had tended to be extremely deferential to the Security Council.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>Former UN corruption fighter <a href="/wiki/James_Wasserstrom" title="James Wasserstrom">James Wasserstrom</a> has also been critical of Ban Ki-moon for attempting to limit the jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Dispute_Tribunal" title="United Nations Dispute Tribunal">UN dispute tribunal</a> following his dismissal from his Kosovo post and lengthy appeals process.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Ban had refused to hand over confidential documents relating to the case to the UN personnel tribunal, despite repeated orders by the court to do so. In relation to another case, Ban was admonished by Judge Michael Adams for "wilful disobedience" for again failing to hand over key documents in an internal promotions dispute.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, Ban was accused of undermining collective bargaining rights of The Staff Coordinating Council, the union representing United Nations staff. Ban unilaterally eliminated the role of the union to negotiate on behalf of the employees and terminated talks when the union protested.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The United Nations champions the right to collective bargaining as a basic human right in its own charter, enacted as the Right to Organise and Collective Bargaining Convention, 1949; Article 1.</p>
<p>International human rights organizations are critical of Ban Ki-moon for lacking accountability over negligent actions by the United Nations. Scientists and journalists conclusively proved that UN peacekeepers from Nepal were the source of the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9313_Haiti_cholera_outbreak" class="mw-redirect" title="2010–13 Haiti cholera outbreak">2010–13 Haiti cholera outbreak</a>, which has killed approximately 9,000 people and infected more than 1 in 20 Haitians. Ban has declared that the legal immunity of the United Nations before national courts should be upheld, though this does not reduce the UN's moral responsibility to overcoming Haiti's cholera epidemic.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Ban is named in a lawsuit challenging UN immunity on behalf of Haitian cholera victims in the U.S. District Court of Manhattan. In January 2015, Judge <a href="/wiki/J._Paul_Oetken" title="J. Paul Oetken">J. Paul Oetken</a> dismissed the case, affirming UN immunity.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> An appeal<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> to Oetken's decision was submitted to the Court in May 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>Much press coverage of Ban has been critical, with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i>, in May 2016, calling him "plodding, protocol-conscious and loth to stand up to the big powers" and "the dullest—and among the worst" secretary-generals.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> An article in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> of July 2010 calls his performance "deplorable," although Ban is defended by some Asian commentators who see his understated presence as more quietly <a href="/wiki/Confucian" class="mw-redirect" title="Confucian">Confucian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> An article in Foreign Policy noted in a profile of Ban that while he would greet world leaders in their native language, he would then read directly from his talking points without small talk. The UN official who reported this style stated, "Quiet diplomacy? He [Ban] displayed no skills for that.”<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2017_presidential_candidacy_speculation">2017 presidential candidacy speculation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 2017 presidential candidacy speculation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/South_Korean_presidential_election,_2017" title="South Korean presidential election, 2017">South Korean presidential election, 2017</a></div>
<p>Until the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/2016_South_Korean_political_scandal" title="2016 South Korean political scandal">2016 South Korean political scandal</a>, Ban was the leading potential candidate for <a href="/wiki/President_of_South_Korea" title="President of South Korea">President of South Korea</a> in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> However, recent polls show <a href="/wiki/Moon_Jae-in" title="Moon Jae-in">Moon Jae-in</a> of the main opposition <a href="/wiki/Minjoo_Party_of_Korea" title="Minjoo Party of Korea">Minjoo Party of Korea</a> in the lead with a support rating of 32.8 percent, while Ban trails in distant second with 15.4 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Although Ban has repeatedly expressed his desires for running, a UN resolution in 1946 says "a Secretary-General should refrain from accepting" any Governmental position "at any rate immediately on retirement."<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Exceptions to the rule have been made in past history with the 1986 election of <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Waldheim" title="Kurt Waldheim">Kurt Waldheim</a> to the post of <a href="/wiki/President_of_Austria" title="President of Austria">President of Austria</a>, although the position is ceremonial in nature.</p>
<p>Contrary to Ban's public comments hinting at any likely run, private reports indicate otherwise. <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jong-pil" title="Kim Jong-pil">Kim Jong-pil</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_South_Korea" title="Prime Minister of South Korea">Prime Minister of South Korea</a>, was reported to say that Ban Ki-moon would announce his candidacy for the presidency shortly after his term as Secretary-General ends.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Ban was originally predicted to run under the conservative <a href="/wiki/Saenuri_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Saenuri Party">Saenuri Party</a>, but President <a href="/wiki/2016_South_Korean_political_scandal" title="2016 South Korean political scandal">Park Geyn-hye's scandal</a> has cast doubts as to which party Ban would run under.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ban returned to South Korea on January 13, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>On February 1, 2017 he announced he would not be a candidate for president.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family">Family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SoniaMbarekAndBanKi-MoonMars2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/SoniaMbarekAndBanKi-MoonMars2016.jpg/220px-SoniaMbarekAndBanKi-MoonMars2016.jpg" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/SoniaMbarekAndBanKi-MoonMars2016.jpg/330px-SoniaMbarekAndBanKi-MoonMars2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/SoniaMbarekAndBanKi-MoonMars2016.jpg/440px-SoniaMbarekAndBanKi-MoonMars2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4879" data-file-height="2837" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SoniaMbarekAndBanKi-MoonMars2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ban Ki-moon and his wife visit the ancient ruins of <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">Carthage</a> in Tunisia, 29 March 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ban Ki-moon met Yoo Soon-taek in 1962 when they were both in high school. Ban was 18 years old, and Yoo Soon-taek was his secondary school's student council president. Ban Ki-moon married Yoo Soon-taek in 1971.</p>
<p>They have three adult children: two daughters and a son.<sup id="cite_ref-Official_Bio_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Bio-27">[27]</a></sup> His elder daughter, Seon-yong, was born in 1972 and now works for the <a href="/wiki/Korea_Foundation" title="Korea Foundation">Korea Foundation</a> in Seoul. Her spouse is a native of India.<sup id="cite_ref-Ban_Ki-moon_family_ties_India_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ban_Ki-moon_family_ties_India-133">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ban_Ki-moon_India_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ban_Ki-moon_India-134">[134]</a></sup> His son Woo-hyun was born in 1974 in India.<sup id="cite_ref-Ban_Ki-moon_family_ties_India_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ban_Ki-moon_family_ties_India-133">[133]</a></sup> He received an MBA from <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Anderson_School_of_Management" title="UCLA Anderson School of Management">Anderson School of Management</a> at <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Los_Angeles" title="University of California, Los Angeles">University of California, Los Angeles</a>, and works for an investment firm in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> His younger daughter, Hyun-hee (born 1976), is a field officer for <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Children%27s_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Children's Fund">UNICEF</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Times12-09_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times12-09-11">[11]</a></sup> After his election as Secretary-General, Ban became an icon in his hometown, where his extended family still resides. Over 50,000 gathered in a soccer stadium in <a href="/wiki/Chungju" title="Chungju">Chungju</a> for celebration of the result. In the months following his election, thousands of practitioners of <a href="/wiki/Geomancy" title="Geomancy">geomancy</a> went to his village to determine how it produced such an important person.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_12-22_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_12-22-12">[12]</a></sup> Ban himself is not a member of any church or religious group<sup id="cite_ref-Corr_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corr-136">[136]</a></sup> and has declined to expound his beliefs: "Now, as Secretary-General, it will not be appropriate at this time to talk about my own belief in any particular religion or god. So maybe we will have some other time to talk about personal matters."<sup id="cite_ref-un.org_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un.org-137">[137]</a></sup> His mother is <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_12-22_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_12-22-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 January 2017, Ban's brother Ban Ki-sang and nephew Bahn Joo-hyun have been indicted on U.S. charges that they engaged in a scheme to bribe a Middle Eastern official in connection with the attempted $800 million sale of a building complex in Vietnam.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personality">Personality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Personality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During his tenure at the South Korean Foreign Ministry, Ban's nickname was <i>jusa</i> (주사), meaning "the administrative clerk". The name was used as both positive and negative: complimenting Ban's attention to detail and administrative skill while deriding what was seen as a lack of charisma and subservience to his superiors.<sup id="cite_ref-Economist10-07_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist10-07-39">[39]</a></sup> The South Korean press corps calls him "the slippery eel" (기름장어), for his ability to dodge questions.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT10-09_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT10-09-13">[13]</a></sup> His peers praise his understated "<a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucian</a> approach",<sup id="cite_ref-Time_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time-25">[25]</a></sup> and he is regarded by many as a "stand-up guy"<sup id="cite_ref-FT10-10_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT10-10-14">[14]</a></sup> and is known for his "easy smile".<sup id="cite_ref-Times12-09_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times12-09-11">[11]</a></sup> After he assumed a post of United Nations secretary general, he is caricatured as "invisible man", "powerless observer", or "nowhere man" for his lack of powerful personality and leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours_and_awards">Honours and awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Honours and awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>Ban Ki-moon was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Service_Merit" title="Order of Service Merit">Order of Service Merit</a>, 1st class, by the government of <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> on three occasions: in 1975, 1986 and 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-Official_Bio_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Bio-27">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li>For his accomplishments as an envoy, he received the <a href="/wiki/Decoration_of_Honour_for_Services_to_the_Republic_of_Austria" title="Decoration of Honour for Services to the Republic of Austria"><i>Grand Decoration of Honour in Gold with Star</i> (4th Cl.) for Services to the Republic of Austria</a> in 2001 <sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li>He was bestowed the Grand Cross of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Rio_Branco" title="Order of Rio Branco">Order of Rio Branco</a> by the government of <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Peru.svg/23px-Flag_of_Peru.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Peru.svg/35px-Flag_of_Peru.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Peru.svg/45px-Flag_of_Peru.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>&#160;: Grand Cross of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Sun_(Peru)" class="mw-redirect" title="Order of the Sun (Peru)">Order of the Sun</a> (Gran Cruz del Sol) (2006)</li>
<li>He was honored with <a href="/wiki/James_A._Van_Fleet_Award" title="James A. Van Fleet Award">James A. Van Fleet Award</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Korea_Society" title="Korea Society">Korea Society</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> for his contributions to friendship between the United States and South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></li>
<li>Ban Ki-moon, in his capacity as Secretary-General of the United Nations, was one of the Olympic Flag carriers of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics opening ceremony">2012 Summer Olympics opening ceremony</a>.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Flag_of_Algeria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Algeria.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Flag_of_Algeria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Algeria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Flag_of_Algeria.svg/45px-Flag_of_Algeria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>&#160;: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Order_of_Merit_(Algeria)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Order of Merit (Algeria) (page does not exist)">National Order of Merit</a> of Algeria</li>
<li>Commemorative Medal of Freedom Heroes of the Republic of Hungary</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg/23px-Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg.png" width="23" height="13" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg/35px-Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg/46px-Flag_of_El_Salvador.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1064" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a>&#160;: Grand Cross with Silver Star of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Jose_Matias_Delgado" class="mw-redirect" title="Order of Jose Matias Delgado">Order of Jose Matias Delgado</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="450" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>&#160;: Grand Cross of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Sikatuna" title="Order of Sikatuna">Order of Sikatuna</a>, Rank of Raja (October 30, 2008)<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg/46px-Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="300" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>&#160;: <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Friendship_(Kazakhstan)" title="Order of Friendship (Kazakhstan)">Order of Friendship</a>, 1st class (2010)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Flag_of_Tajikistan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Tajikistan.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Flag_of_Tajikistan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Tajikistan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Flag_of_Tajikistan.svg/46px-Flag_of_Tajikistan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a>&#160;: Order of Ismoili Samoni – 2010</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Flag_of_Burkina_Faso.svg/23px-Flag_of_Burkina_Faso.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Flag_of_Burkina_Faso.svg/35px-Flag_of_Burkina_Faso.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Flag_of_Burkina_Faso.svg/45px-Flag_of_Burkina_Faso.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a>&#160;: Grand Cross of the National Order of <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a> (2008)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire.svg/23px-Flag_of_C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire.svg/35px-Flag_of_C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire.svg/45px-Flag_of_C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="300" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a>&#160;: Grand Officer of the National Order of Ivory Coast (2008)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Flag_of_Monaco.svg/19px-Flag_of_Monaco.svg.png" width="19" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Flag_of_Monaco.svg/29px-Flag_of_Monaco.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Flag_of_Monaco.svg/38px-Flag_of_Monaco.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>&#160;: Grand Cross of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint-Charles" title="Order of Saint-Charles">Order of Saint-Charles</a> (2013)<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/45px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>&#160;: Grand Golden Order of the City of <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> (2013)</li>
<li>Ban Ki-moon, in his capacity as Secretary-General of the United Nations, was one of the Olympic Torch carriers of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics" title="2014 Winter Olympics">2014 Winter Olympic Games</a>.</li>
<li>He accepted the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Tipperary_International_Peace_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Tipperary International Peace Award">Tipperary International Peace Award</a>, described as "Ireland's outstanding award for humanitarian work",<sup id="cite_ref-TIPA-Indo01a_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TIPA-Indo01a-148">[148]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/County_Tipperary" title="County Tipperary">County Tipperary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> in May 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-TIPA2014-RTE01a_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TIPA2014-RTE01a-149">[149]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>&#160;: Grand Cross of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Netherlands_Lion" title="Order of the Netherlands Lion">Order of the Netherlands Lion</a> (19 April 2016)<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>&#160;: He was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Friendship" title="Order of Friendship">Order of Friendship</a> by Vladimir Putin, "for his special role in strengthening peace, friendship, cooperation and mutual understanding between nations" (8 June 2016)<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/23px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/35px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/46px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="500" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>&#160;: Grand Cross of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Liberator_General_San_Mart%C3%ADn" title="Order of the Liberator General San Martín">Order of the Liberator General San Martín</a> (2016).</li>
<li>Ban Ki-moon, in his capacity as Secretary-General of the United Nations, was one of the Olympic Torch carriers of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Summer Olympics</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honorary_degrees">Honorary degrees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ban_Ki-moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Honorary degrees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Honorary Doctor of Public Service degree from <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_College_Park" title="University of Maryland, College Park">University of Maryland, College Park</a> on 17 October 2016<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></li>
<li>Honorary Doctor of Humane Letters degree from <a href="/wiki/Loyola_Marymount_University" title="Loyola Marymount University">Loyola Marymount University</a> on 6 April 2016<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></li>
<li>Honorary Doctor of Laws degree of <a href="/wiki/The_University_of_Auckland" class="mw-redirect" title="The University of Auckland">The University of Auckland</a> on 3 September 2014<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></li>
<li>Honorary doctorate in Human Letters degree of <a href="/wiki/Fairleigh_Dickinson_University" title="Fairleigh Dickinson University">Fairleigh Dickinson University</a> on 10 September 2008<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></li>
<li>Honorary doctorate from <a href="/wiki/Seoul_National_University" title="Seoul National University">Seoul National University</a> (2008)</li>
<li>Doctor Honoris Causa by the <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_San_Marcos" title="National University of San Marcos">National University of San Marcos</a>, the main university in Peru and the oldest of the Americas (2011)</li>
<li>Doctor of Laws Degree Honoris Causa by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Philippines_College_of_Law" title="University of the Philippines College of Law">College of Law</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Philippines_Diliman" title="University of the Philippines Diliman">University of the Philippines Diliman</a>, the national university of the country, in 2008</li>
<li>Honorary Doctor by the <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Mongolia" title="National University of Mongolia">National University of Mongolia</a> in 2009<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></li>
<li>"Doctors of Letters" by <a href="/wiki/Jamia_Millia_Islamia" title="Jamia Millia Islamia">Jamia Millia Islamia</a> in New Delhi<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></li>
<li>Honorary doctorates in law from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Malta" title="University of Malta">University of Malta</a> (2009) and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington" title="University of Washington">University of Washington</a> (2009)</li>
<li>Honorary doctorate of public service from <a href="/wiki/Denver_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Denver University">Denver University</a> (2013)<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></li>
<li>Honorary doctorate from <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">Georgetown University</a> (2015)<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></li>
<li>Honorary doctorate from <a href="/wiki/Katholieke_Universiteit_Leuven" title="Katholieke Universiteit Leuven">Katholieke Universiteit Leuven</a> (2015)<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></li>
<li>Doctor honoris causa from <a href="/wiki/Comenius_University" title="Comenius University">Comenius University</a> (2015)<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></li>
<li>Degree of Doctor of Civil Law Honoris Causa from <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mauritius" title="University of Mauritius">University of Mauritius</a> (2016)<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></li>
<li>Honorary Doctor of Laws from <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> (2016)<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></li>
<li>Honorary Degree from <a href="/wiki/Marymount_Manhattan_College" title="Marymount Manhattan College">Marymount Manhattan College</a> (2016)<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></li>
<li>Doctor honoris causa from <a href="/wiki/Panth%C3%A9on-Sorbonne_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Panthéon-Sorbonne University">Panthéon-Sorbonne University</a> (2016)</li>
</ul>
